<Text>My wife and I were on our honeymoon and were very hungry and craving good Mexican food. We came to this restaurant and the waiter have us a basket full of tortilla chips and a bowl of salsa, got our drinks, and then later got our order, my wife and I finished the chips and the salsa, which was very soupy by the way, and never got anymore. We normally always have chips and salsa to eat while wait for our food, but ok. We ordered fijite for two and, boy was it disappointing. It was not seasoned right. On the menu, it said it was somewhere around $22. But when we got our ticket, we charged $30 plus drinks and tax which totaled near $40. I consulted with our waiter and he, pretty gruffly, told me "you ordered fijete for two" and I told him "It said $22 on the menu and it says $30 on the ticket." Well, he corrected the error, but we waited for him to come back and get our ticket and let us pay it. We just left the ticket on the table with the exact amount of money due and left. Needless to say, he didn't get a tip from us.
So overall, no refill on the chips, we got overcharged, as well as the ones at the next table over, we waited too long to pay our bill, and the food wasn't good.< /Text>< gmapID>

<Gmap_id>0x80ec13976973f1f7:0x8a3ea48bb95ff029<//Gmap_id>< text>
Being new to the area, I looked in the local Yellow Pages (People still use those? Yes, some people do.) to find a Mexican food restaurant. The ad stated something about "Voted best salsa bar in Santa Maria!" Well that sounds encouraging, doesn't it? Who doesn't like a good salsa bar. How many salsas do they have, I wondered? With visions of perhaps as many as six varieties of exotic flavors dancing in my head, I walked in the door with my family.

It's a quite narrow restaurant, being in the corner of a strip mall, and laid out quite awkwardly. At the back I found their salsa bar, with a grand total of two salsa bowls: one large bowl for the mild salsa, one small bowl for the spicy salsa. In fact, both bowls were fairly small, and I guess technically it was indeed a salsa bar, but to me it barely qualified. If this is the best in the area, it is only because nobody else has one. Seriously, I'm much more impressed with El Pollo Loco's selection.

Ah well, brushing aside the disappointment we moved onto dinner. The first time, I ordered hard shell tacos. They were pretty good, and I had a good feeling about developing a liking for this place. The beans and rice on the side were ... well, they were beans and rice. They're never that great, but some places somehow serve better than others. These folks are not among the top with their beans and rice, but they will do. The rest of the family consumed their food, but the consensus was that it was serviceable food.

The next time I ordered a chile verde burrito. It was bland and disappointing. I ended up dumping salsa and Tapatio all over it to try to liven things up a bit, but it really didn't help much. To top it off, I ended up with a nasty upset stomach that night. I wouldn't say the food made me sick. Hey, it's Mexican food, sometimes that happens right? Still, I haven't been back. It seems the risk of upset stomach outweighs the tasty factor for this particular restaurant.

These days I find myself cooking my own food when I get the hankering for Mexican flavors rather than head over to this place for a ho-hum burrito. I may return soon to try their hard tacos again, but don't hold your breath.< /text>

< review>
I've heard about Walker Burger for a little while, finally had a chance to stop in and try for myself. Very good burger, juicy and delicious! Love their big steak fries too! Great staff, very friendly! Plenty to choose from on the menu to satisfy nearly anyone. Really enjoyed the outdoor seating area, very scenic and relaxing.

When you're traveling Hwy 395 through Coleville make sure to take time out and stop by Walker Burger!< /review>

I remember when Walker Burger opened up in 1982.  You could place your order and have it delivered to Coleville High School just in time for lunch.  I haven't had Walker Burger in many years, as I moved away and don't get back there too often.  My husband and I went hiking outside Bridgeport, CA and decided to stop and get hamburgers,  french fries, Sierra Mist, and a chocolate chip milkshake.  üçîüçüüç¶ü•§

<review>I would give it a solid 5 stars except they implemented a new dumb policy.  For the past decade, we ALWAYS save our appetite for a Walker Burger when driving the 395. One on way down to So Cal and another on the way back to Lake Tahoe. In addition to the great tasting burger, their backyard is fun and relaxing.
My ONLY complaint is they now surcharge 3% on credit cards. I understand trying to cut costs, but to guilt customers into paying cash only limits how much customers are going to spend with cash. What is next? ,50¬¢ fee to use the bathroom? Parking fees? It's 18¬¢ on a burger. Just raise the price a quarter and let customers pay their preferred way without guilt. And take ALL major credit cards! My company pays my business meals when I use the American Express Corporate card. By saving 18 cents, you lost my splurge on milk shake and fries.  Not sure if they are trying to avoid paying taxes or just being short business minded.

< Text>
Decent apartment complex. Donna and most of the people in the front office are very friendly and helpful. They have a bunch of pools and spas which are very well kept, so that was a bonus. The only real complaint I have is that they charge too much for rent. $2029 a month as of Jan 1st, 2018 for a studio apartment on a 7 month lease, while there are much newer and nicer complexes in RC that charge around the same. But, if you need to find a place quickly like I did, then they will make it happen. They definitely are doing a great job when it comes to customer service and are easy to work with.

Edit - I thought I would give a complete picture since management replied to my review. I currently pay $1428 per month on a 6 month lease.

My renewal offer was as follows:
Studio Apartment
7 Months @ $2029 per month
10 Months @ $1982 per month
13 Months @  $1463 per month

I'd just like to be fair, there is quite a discount for a longer lease. I just personally don't like to be locked down to one location for more than 8 months or so, but you may be different. I also have updated my review from 4 stars to 5 stars because I realized how ridiculous it was to knock off a star because of the rent price.< /Text>

We were told that the rate would not increase after 7 months and is was better for us because it gave us flexibility.  This was not true, the rent did in fact increase after the 7 months by about $200 ($1150 increased to $1348).  We were not told of any mandatory fees that would be charge at the time of move out. The apartment was a good size for the price we were paying and the location was great for us.  Unfortunately our apartment reeked of cigarette smoke from the previous tenant. <Name>C. Christian Gill< /Name><Resp>{'time': 1606854134624, 'text': 'Thanks Christian!  Was happy to help someone out in the North Bay!'}<//Resp>< Text>
I found Trevor via mutual client, and after reading a few of his reviews on Yelp and on Google, I thought: "what kind of man has a PERFECT five star score after 50 Yelp reviews?? What type of sorcery is this?"  Nope - no sorcery, and yep Trevor just is that good.

I had been working under a simple DBA for a couple years, made the decision to incorporate and having read one ENTIRE self help book on corporate law I was of course an expert so I was hesitant to employ someone for that which I could effortlessly do myself.  (yes, that's sarcasm, for those in the back)

I worked on my bylaws for months; going back and forth between the bylaws and articles - changing this or that, rephrasing the legalese as best as I knew how, tediously researching each word one by one as I sludged through the process.  (yeah I know sludged is not technically a word, but it feels so right)

The realization that I needed help was not an acute apprehension - I would say it was more of a dull, painful brooding like walking with a thorn in your shoe for miles before finally realizing you can simply stop and remove the thorn. (duh)

Two minutes on the phone with Trevor was all I needed to know that the incorporation process was secure.  I didn't even ask all my questions - I didn't need to; Trevor was smart, responsive, accessible, resourceful and down to earth. These are more or less the qualities I look for whenever I need to engage in any business endeavor.

Conversely, all those lawyers who love to wave their fancy diplomas around like flags, who have SAT scores posted on their websites, an office wall full of awards or the fact that some highfalutin lawyer markets himself as a MENSA member means exactly nothing to me, except that I would expect the MENSA membership cost to be built into the fee scale -- no thank you.

However, the qualities Trevor possesses inherently, all of which are plainly evident, mean everything to me as a discerning businessman because they basically guarantee success - I knew right away Trevor was going to make sure every thing was taken care of, which really took the pressure off of me so I was able to focus on process, the books, marketing, etc etc etc.

After deciding to hire Trevor to incorporate my company I had an overwhelming feeling of relief - THANK GOD. I have never been happier about spending $$ as I did the day I hired Trevor Caudle -  KNOWING that everything would be done correctly and that nothing would be overlooked: PRICELESS. Thanks Trevor for the peace of mind.< /Text>

I wish I hadn't grown up before cell phones were commonly sold online a shipped to your door. I got used to going in to phone stores to buy cell phones and while I have adapted well to most aspects of modern Amazon/Facebook fueled life, the damn cell phone store is my kryptonite. I can usually find better prices online but for some reason my stupid brain stops me from ordering and drags me down to the T-Mobile store where I fumble with phones attached to the wall with cables. Some even work. After looking at all the phones I will inevitably decide on the one I saw online and then resolve to go back home and order it. Before I can get out the door, my scumbag brain convinces me that since I drove to the store, maybe I should just shell out a few extra bucks and go home the phone that day. After a little back and forth with the sales guy we work out the details and it then takes an unusually long time for him to finish up at the register. At the end if it all the salesman runs my card and then informs me that they don't have my phone in stock and that it will be arriving by mail within the next week. I go home and wait for the package and try to figure out why I paid more to get it later than when Amazon could have had it to me. Damn it! Oh well, the store is nice and clean and the people are nice and they are no more or less helpful than the staff at any other cell phone store in America. Good selection of accessories.< /review>
